< text>
My first encounter with this practice was when I was in the hospital, in 2013, with a perforated colon (which I could have died from but my original gastroenterologist failed to tell me that). That original gastroenterologist came to my room, introduced me to one of the three doctors in this practice (which after this many years, I don't remember which one), and announce he was leaving the country for several weeks and they would take care of me. And they did. After being in the hospital for about 2+ weeks, the decision I had to make was to have immediate surgery which would incur a colostomy bag, or try to wait as long as possible to let the area heal up a bit first. Dr. Yu recommended that I wait, while the surgeon wanted to go in and cut right then. I decided to go home on IVs and wait, and the fact that I did made a huge difference when I ultimately went in for surgery about a month later.  I didn't have to have the colostomy bag after having the colectomy (resection)! Since then I have seen Dr. Bemanian a couple of times for appointments, and he is very personable and seems to listen. I now have an endoscopy and colonoscopy scheduled with Dr. Lee, so if there is an update to this I will post later. I have every confidence with this group. Phone calls are usually returned fairly promptly, although getting scheduled for a procedure might be a bit slow, for which I took off one star. Don't think you can do too much better than this group to be honest. My original gastro never followed up on my 2 stays in the hospital within 3+ months, but his office called me a year later to schedule a colonoscopy. When I told them I was with another group because of his non follow-up, he never called to discuss it with me. Guess he didn't need my business!<//text>

< review>
Located on Lincoln Blvd., between Washington and Venice Blvd. is a slightly hidden shop between all the others that line the street, but at first glance of their display case, your eyes will widen and your salivary glands go into overdrive. *Hint- all desserts labeled as a ‚ÄúSaint‚Äù are gluten-free, and can either be low in sugar or fats; and also offer Paleo diet, and Vegan options.

Cannoli- Filled with peanut butter and strawberry jam, then topped with chopped pistachio nuts. Man, oh man, did it ever feel like the better parts of my chubby childhood brought back into the present when I took my first bite into this lip smacking cannoli. Good thing I‚Äôve developed somewhat of a bit of self control, or else I would‚Äôve annihilated the whole lot of these.

Red Velvet Cupcakes-Yes, I know. What‚Äôs the big deal with red velvet, EVERYBODY‚ÄôS got it on their menus, right? Well, in their case, however it is that their recipe is  modified, it‚Äôs working. The batter itself is lighter, crumbles beautifully, and its moisture content is higher than the other red velvets I‚Äôve tried anywhere else. Also, paired with the creamiest frosting that is so on point, my fat ass was ready to buy it on the side like a junkie wanting to score a fix.

Bourbon Croissant Bread Pudding- Warm and fresh out of the oven. Amazing flavor with the diced apples and cinnamon infused within as if an apple strudel and a brule√©d French toast had a drunken threesome with a rich and buttery croissant, then nine months later this bread pudding was born. I must have it again.

Gluten Free Blackberry Goat Cheese Cheesecake ‚Äì As soon as I read the description, I had to try it. It seemed like this particular cheesecake was specifically made for my sister. It is rich and decadent in flavors, without worry of it affecting your health. The tartness of the berries is balanced out by the sweetened, creaminess of the goat cheese. You definitely get hypnotized by swirls of the blackberry infusion within the cake itself. Well worth trying at least once in your life‚Ä¶ or twice.

Gluten Free Caramel Cheesecake ‚Äì A soft and crumbly crust that is covered with a thick, insanely good cheesecake topped with Dulce de Leche, or caramel sauce for you non-food speaking adventurers. It is also garnished with hefty pieces of peanut brittle putting other candy/dessert shops to shame. I tried to pace myself eating this beauty so it would last me for at least two days..Was gone by the end of the first night.< /review>

< review>
Awesome new, modern tasting room. The tasting experience is focused mainly on Walt Chardonnays and Pinot Noir. You will taste wines from a variety of appellations including Willamette Valley, Oregon to as far South as Santa Barbara, CA. The main winery,  Hall Wines in St. Helena, Napa Valley, has additional varietals you won't want to miss either.</review>

<review>The food was decent. You can tell it's fresh and I always appreciate when a Mexican place has al pastor and lengua in addition to the classic carnitas steak and chicken. Prices are also pretty good: good size burrito for 7-8 bucks So that's the good things about this place. Here's the bad:

1 they serve everything with one time use cutlery and styrofoam plates so you're basically GUARENTEED to eat particles of styrofoam. You have maybe 10 tables with 4 seats each, you can't afford to provide your guests proper tableware?

2 cheese, sour cream, and guacamole are 75c extra. Guacamole I understand, but you're telling me I get almost a dollar worth of cheese or sour cream on my order? Give me a break.

3 credit cards are charged an extra 50c. This is just annoying. I understand you prefer cash but this is 2016.

4 almost forgot. No chips no salsa, those cost extra. Can't stand places that don't do this. Even Sharkeys gives free chips and salsa.

In summary, I think it's a decent place that has potential but until some changes are made it'll be hard for me to justify coming back. Too bad, I was looking for a good Mexican place I could eat at for lunch near my job in Simi Valley. The search continues.<//review>< UserId.>

<rating>1< /rating>< review>
I was attracted to this store after reading their weekly add.  The ribeye steaks $4.95 a pound.  A great price for ribeye steaks.  I was impressed by the variety and the quantity of displayed meat in the meat department.  I was also impressed by the size of the ribeye steak on display.  Was it bizarre that one ribeye steak was at the top of the pile of ribeyes and near the display window for the consumer to see, while all other ribeyes were covered and not visible?  I was helped quickly at the meat counter.  This has been a good experience up until this point.  When I got home and unpacked the ribeyes to prepare for the bbq.  I was disappointed.  Quickly the disappointment turned into a feeling of bamboozlement.  I replayed in my mind the nice lady at the meat counter packing the ribeyes in the bag.  There were three steaks she packed the first two steaks and lastly a very nice large ribeye steak on top.  The two steaks packed first by the nice lady look like less expensive chuck steak. What is this???

Is this the way they do business?  Have you been bamboozled by this store?  No thank you State Foods!  I will stick to shopping at quality stores.  I prefer not to be bamboozled.<//review>
